<span id="freeTextContainer11148832616673595563">Public health care is one of the most important issues in America today. Now Robin Cook, the bestselling master of medical suspense, confronts this controversial subject with an all-too-possible scenario as powerful--and terrifying--as his groundbreaking blockbuster, <strong>Coma</strong>...With its state-of-the-art facility and peaceful Vermont setting, the Bartlet Community Hospital seem</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11148832616673595563">Public health care is one of the most important issues in America today. Now Robin Cook, the bestselling master of medical suspense, confronts this controversial subject with an all-too-possible scenario as powerful--and terrifying--as his groundbreaking blockbuster, <strong>Coma</strong>...With its state-of-the-art facility and peaceful Vermont setting, the Bartlet Community Hospital seemed like a dream come true. It offered doctors David and Angela Wilson new career opportunities, a chance to work within an enlightened system of "Managed care" --and a perfect place to raise their daughter, who suffered from cystic fibrosis. But then, one by one, their dreams turned to nightmares. And day by day, their patients began to die...<br /><br /><br /><em>Also see: Alternate Cover Editions for this ISBN [ACE] </em><br /><strong>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/872238">ACE #1</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_375779474">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/375779474" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2456844-theresa-leone-davidson" class="left imgcol" title="Theresa Leone Davidson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1248728177p2/2456844.jpg" alt="Theresa Leone Davidson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/375779474?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 26, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2456844-theresa-leone-davidson" class="user" title="Theresa Leone Davidson">Theresa Leone Davidson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/872238.Fatal_Cure" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer375779474">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16924857952473010393">I continue to read Robin Cook's novels because they are always suspenseful, with clearly drawn characters, some of whom are the goody-goodies, and others who are the villains. Also he brings something a little different to the thriller by writing about medical situations, an area he knows about as he is a physician. Fatal Cure, insofar as all of this is concerned, is no exception. I read it in only two days so clearly it is a suspenseful story. However, I never think of his novels as being worth</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16924857952473010393">I continue to read Robin Cook's novels because they are always suspenseful, with clearly drawn characters, some of whom are the goody-goodies, and others who are the villains. Also he brings something a little different to the thriller by writing about medical situations, an area he knows about as he is a physician. Fatal Cure, insofar as all of this is concerned, is no exception. I read it in only two days so clearly it is a suspenseful story. However, I never think of his novels as being worthy of more than two and a half stars. Wooden dialogue, characters who are often too good or too evil, unlike most real people, and endings that don't quite tie up all the loose strings (well, DID Dr. Portland kill himself or was he murdered????) and, in this particular novel, I have a few specific complaints: the family is offered jobs in a seemingly idyllic town in Vermont and all of a sudden, in one week, Boston, the big, bad city, is a nightmare, with break-ins, sixth graders selling drugs, etc., etc., and conveniently, Cook forgets why people live in big cities and put up with such issues, things like the museums, the nightlife, the cultural activities, the restaurants. In Fatal Cure the family moves to a fictional Vermont town with exactly one movie theatre and two restaurants. That's idyllic? Also, the couple in the story, two of the stupider characters Cook has made up, are both doctors, and the wife has the more lucrative position and earns twice as much as her husband. I suppose that makes Cook think he is liberated, to write such a character, but guess who does 90% of the cooking in the story? Guess who is accused by her husband, at least ten times throughout the story, of being a hysteric? They find a dead body in their basement and he accuses her of being hysterical. C'mon now, she wasn't hysterical enough. Nevertheless, the suspense is why I don't just stop reading his novels. I just wish, after all these years, and all his books, Cook had improved some of the more flawed aspects of his writing. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16924857952473010393">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer3284120980500474039">I don't expect high art from Robin Cook. However, his other books tend to have satisfying endings. This one ended rather abruptly and the shadow of doubt over the main characters was never resolved. Sure, it may be more true to real life than everything tied up in a neat package, but hey, if you're going to make me fear ever going to the doctor again, give me the bow. </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer75684556">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12107716971928763522">Robin Cook was an MD, and he is apparently disgruntled with the<br />way the medical field is managed. I don't disagree with him, but reading about it was not much fun. The plot was a bit far-fetched, and the characters were a bit flat. I won't say they were two-dimensional, but I wouldn't go three, either. Is there a 2.5 dimension?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6446049791764496485">I deleted this review by accident but I wanted to say a couple of words about the book. Read it last September 2012 as a new author for me. The book was slow at 1st but picked up steam and really sent the reader in unexpected twists and turns.<br /><br />While I thought a story based on healthcare would be boring it proved me wrong. The story was good to borderline great. The underlying problem that is causing medical health histaria is so on the mark with this book that it left me wondering about my own me</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6446049791764496485">I deleted this review by accident but I wanted to say a couple of words about the book. Read it last September 2012 as a new author for me. The book was slow at 1st but picked up steam and really sent the reader in unexpected twists and turns.<br /><br />While I thought a story based on healthcare would be boring it proved me wrong. The story was good to borderline great. The underlying problem that is causing medical health histaria is so on the mark with this book that it left me wondering about my own medical care I have gotten in past years.<br /><br />I found myself struggling with the fact that this hospital's medical administration found they could "kill" a few terminal, or near terminal, people and no-one would notice all in the name of "PROFIT". It seems to be too close to reality that I shudder to think that it may actually be happening and no-one really knows it. Goes to show you that you have to always be questioning what is being done to our love ones in the name of humanity and medical treatment.<br /><br />A must read for people who DON'T believe that the "medical administration machine" is more concerned about making a great profit ahead of our individual medical care is going to find it hard to put this book down.<br /><br />Would I read it again: yes. Would I recommend it to others: yes.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_144228145">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144228145" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4396469-jayme-damm" class="left imgcol" title="Jayme Damm"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1294517519p2/4396469.jpg" alt="Jayme Damm" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/144228145?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 28, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4396469-jayme-damm" class="user" title="Jayme Damm">Jayme Damm</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/308274.Fatal_Cure" title="Unknown Binding 9780330337021" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer144228145">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15563507697831765089">In this book, Robin Cook did an amazing job of keeping you on the edge of your seat. The Wilson’s family moved to Bartlet after a serious of unfortunate events in their life. Bankruptcy and a robbery were just a part of the life they were living. They moved to Bartlet in hopes that it would be a better life for them but something different than what they were asking for. The first few days were awesome until things around the town started seeming suspicious. A suicide of a doctor occurs because</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15563507697831765089">In this book, Robin Cook did an amazing job of keeping you on the edge of your seat. The Wilson’s family moved to Bartlet after a serious of unfortunate events in their life. Bankruptcy and a robbery were just a part of the life they were living. They moved to Bartlet in hopes that it would be a better life for them but something different than what they were asking for. The first few days were awesome until things around the town started seeming suspicious. A suicide of a doctor occurs because all his patients are dying for no apparent reason. When this starts showing up for David Wilson he doesn’t know what to do. A murder crime scene is made in the basement of their house when they find a dead body behind of handmade wall. But this is just the beginning…<br />Robin Cook had a great way of showing you through words that dreams aren’t always good. Don’t expect too much out of situation because sometimes it can turn on you and you’ll be the one at stake. I loved the way she put the characters in a situation that may actually happen in life. Thousands of people are murdered and hidden every year and in this book that one body changes their whole life. I liked the way you could easier put yourself in a characters position and try to feel what they might have felt. If I had a choice to recommend this book to others, I defiantly would. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15563507697831765089">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17746153705694422079">Hasta podría decir que no me gustó, pero sólo es por el final, así que decidí dejarlo en dos estrellas.<br />La razón más fuerte para que no me gustara este libro fue que durante todas las páginas le da vueltas y más vueltas a las muertes misteriosas en el hospital, todo para que al final dejara de escribir de repente. Encontraron a los malos en un par de páginas, se acabó todo y a la siguiente página ya eran cuatro meses después y la historia estaba estancada.<br />Otra cosa mala es la forma en que suceden</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17746153705694422079">Hasta podría decir que no me gustó, pero sólo es por el final, así que decidí dejarlo en dos estrellas.<br />La razón más fuerte para que no me gustara este libro fue que durante todas las páginas le da vueltas y más vueltas a las muertes misteriosas en el hospital, todo para que al final dejara de escribir de repente. Encontraron a los malos en un par de páginas, se acabó todo y a la siguiente página ya eran cuatro meses después y la historia estaba estancada.<br />Otra cosa mala es la forma en que suceden los diálogos. La marca de Robin Cook, en mi experiencia, es incluir muchos detalles médicos a sus novelas. Es una cosa buena, a veces esos detalles estuvieron bien incluidos y me gustaron, pero en la mayoría de los casos la forma en que dichos detalles aparecen es en una conversación. En este libros hay dos médicos-algo así- que tienen una niña de como ocho años-no recuerdo-, por lo que hay montones de diálogos entre ellos. Cómo no, la niña pregunta y pregunta y ellos responden y responden. Los diálogos así no se me hicieron muy naturales. Ni entre la familia, ni el de ellos con las otras personas.<br /><br />Y están los personajes. Si no me equivoco, el libro fue escrito en 1994, ¿cuando el mundo era más simple? Al menos eso parece, porque los personajes de este libro son totalmente unidimensionales. David quejándose de la histérica de su esposa, luego de que trataran de matarla, encontraran muertos, violadores y locura...Y blablabla, no tiene caso hablar de esto.<br /><br />En resumen, esta es una novela sobre cómo de horrible es el sistema de salud americano y qué malvadas pueden ser las personas cuando se trata de dinero. Más un bonus de medicina e intrigas criminales. Está bien para pasar el rato, si no quieres pensar demasiado y sí aprender cositas para soltar durante un vacío de conversación.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17746153705694422079">...more</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7255446-megan-stewart" class="user" title="Megan Stewart">Megan Stewart</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who love thrillers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Megan by: </span>
      School library discarded it, so I took it home
  </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1278078200">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12560135308233443175">Honestly, I had a love-hate relationship with this book the entire time I was reading it. Mostly hate-hate, though. I don't think I would have gotten through the novel had I not been trying to escape end of the year homework and studying for finals. It was so long and tedious, and just plain boring for more than half the book. And I am not kidding when I say half the book. Nothing. Happens. At. All. It's, like, 500 pages and 200 of those could be thrown away, thanks to the excess and unnecessary</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12560135308233443175">Honestly, I had a love-hate relationship with this book the entire time I was reading it. Mostly hate-hate, though. I don't think I would have gotten through the novel had I not been trying to escape end of the year homework and studying for finals. It was so long and tedious, and just plain boring for more than half the book. And I am not kidding when I say half the book. Nothing. Happens. At. All. It's, like, 500 pages and 200 of those could be thrown away, thanks to the excess and unnecessary details Mr. Cook likes to add in there. I'm all for description, but when the author basically writes intricate paragraphs about the weather or how pleasant the town was repeatedly, all I can think is, "You think you're so smart, don't you?" My favorite line that displays his arrogant diction: "...he commenced his walk". Commenced? Seriously? What couldn't you just have said, "He continued to walk", or something less formal and snooty? <br /><br />I'll give him this however: when the plot starts going, you can't pull yourself away from the book. And... that happens, like, five times throughout Fatal Cure, and each example is spread out from the others. I was really excited at the end, because of this, and for a few chapters I thought maybe I'd end up giving it three stars instead of two. I was wrong, unfortunately. The "disease" turned out to be something stupid, the killer was just plain dumb, and the resolution was so... cliche. And not even in a good way, where you feel all warm inside while knowing you're being pathetic. <br /><br />All in all, I'm glad I read this book -- just so I can say I finished such a monsterous read -- but I can't say I enjoyed it much. I'll admit this guy's pretty darn smart, and I still applaud him for writing and publishing several novels (as well as starting his own genre, or so I've heard). I mean, how much can I really judge an author's work when I can barely sit down and write a chapter of my own story? Heh.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12560135308233443175">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1369648105">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1369648105" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/45609815-jorge-mart-nez-niebles-retrospecktiva-books" class="left imgcol" title="Jorge Martínez Niebles (Retrospecktiva Books)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452384843p2/45609815.jpg" alt="Jorge Martínez Niebles (Retrospecktiva Books)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1369648105?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 28, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/45609815-jorge-mart-nez-niebles-retrospecktiva-books" class="user" title="Jorge Martínez Niebles (Retrospecktiva Books)">Jorge Martínez Niebles (Retrospecktiva Books)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/872238.Fatal_Cure" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1369648105">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7652326462350965514">Había comprado esta novela hace ya unos tres años y el librero que me atendió me dijo que era una obra sumamente interesante, con una calidad de suspenso casi igual a la de otros autores como Stephen King (aunque no estoy 100% seguro de comparar una cosa con la otra, pues cada quien es único en su estilo) Cabe decir que la compré de segunda, porque en aquella época, mis estudios frustrados de diseño gráfico no me permitían comprar libros nuevos.<br /><br />No en balde, fue hasta hace una semana que acabo de</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7652326462350965514">Había comprado esta novela hace ya unos tres años y el librero que me atendió me dijo que era una obra sumamente interesante, con una calidad de suspenso casi igual a la de otros autores como Stephen King (aunque no estoy 100% seguro de comparar una cosa con la otra, pues cada quien es único en su estilo) Cabe decir que la compré de segunda, porque en aquella época, mis estudios frustrados de diseño gráfico no me permitían comprar libros nuevos.<br /><br />No en balde, fue hasta hace una semana que acabo de leérmelo ya que lo tuve desde entonces, apilado en mi repisa y no me había motivado a leerlo ¡Y hasta pensaba en revenderlo! De haberlo hecho, no estaría aquí, escribiendo esta reseña.<br /><br />Fatal Cure (Tratamiento Letal, en español) relata la historia de Angela y David Wilson, una pareja de médicos, ambos padres de una pequeña llamada Nikki (quien sufre de fibrosis quística) recientemente se establecen en un hermoso pueblo llamado Vermont, en cuyo hospital, fueron admitidos bajo grandes promesas de un paraíso en la Tierra con una paga bastante atractiva y con la que podrían solventar sus necesidades y su principal prioridad: su hijita enferma.<br /><br />Sin embargo, conforme el tiempo vaya avanzando, ambos descubrirán que hay una mano oculta tras una extraña cadena de muertes de pacientes que presentan una sintomatología para nada ajena entre cada uno de ellos, a la sazón de que varias agresiones sexuales en los alrededores del hospital de Bartlet contra las trabajadoras del lugar podrán sobre alerta a las directivas del sitio. Lo más preocupante del caso, es que la propia junta directiva se hace la de la ''vista gorda'' ante las protestas de David, quien poco a poco se sumirá en la desesperación al no comprender la causa real de estas muertes injustas de todos aquellos a quienes sirve, por el simple placer de ayudar a los necesitados. De igual forma, concluirá que hay cierta complicidad entre las directivas del hospital y un dudoso sistema administrativo que a más de un lector, se le antojará anti-ético y algo para nada lejano a una mafia de la salud.<br /><br />Por si fuera poco, la misteriosa desaparición del ex-director del hospital obligará por su parte a Angela, a emprender una cruzada por descubrir la verdad y esto le acarreará diversas situaciones que pondrán en peligro su integridad.<br /><br />La novela es una muestra de la actual realidad de la salud (al menos aquí en Colombia, donde la corrupción está descaradamente presente en todo, pese a que su autor es estadounidense) en el que la vida de un paciente significa mucho menos que el dinero o los recursos de un sistema deficiente, y por tanto, no es de extrañar que el peor asesino es aquel que sabiendo lo que debe hacer por otro, lo omite y eso es algo que se verá muy claramente en el desarrollo de los hechos. Lamentablemente, la salud se ha convertido en un negocio que beneficia a muy pocos en el mundo. Una novela de suspenso y momentos cargados de tensión, que nos hará conmiserarnos con las frustraciones de sus protagonistas y llenará de rabia nuestros corazones con cada una de las situaciones injustas que allí se presentarán. Pero con el alivio de que los malos siempre pierden y de que cada quien ''cosecha lo que siembra''.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7652326462350965514">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18185089646174518611">Bartlet est une charmante petite ville américaine. Pourtant, David et Angela Wilson, deux jeunes médecins plein d'espoir et de confiance dans la science, vont bien vite regretter de s'y être installés.<br /><br /> Ils commencent par découvrir que, plus qu'ailleurs, mieux vaut y être riche et en bonne santé que pauvre et malade : on réprimande les médecins prescrivant des actes jugés onéreux et les remboursements sont plus qu'aléatoires. <br /><br />Plus grave : les malades de David commencent à mourir un peu trop rapid</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18185089646174518611">Bartlet est une charmante petite ville américaine. Pourtant, David et Angela Wilson, deux jeunes médecins plein d'espoir et de confiance dans la science, vont bien vite regretter de s'y être installés.<br /><br /> Ils commencent par découvrir que, plus qu'ailleurs, mieux vaut y être riche et en bonne santé que pauvre et malade : on réprimande les médecins prescrivant des actes jugés onéreux et les remboursements sont plus qu'aléatoires. <br /><br />Plus grave : les malades de David commencent à mourir un peu trop rapidement et le cadavre de l'ancien directeur de l'hôpital ne trouve rien de mieux à faire que de réapparaître dans la cave des Wilson. <br /><br />Très vite, David et Angela sont eux-mêmes menacés... <br /><br /><br />Chirurgien de formation, c'est tout naturellement que l'Américain Robin Cook (à ne pas confondre avec son homonyme anglais) a fait du thriller médical son genre de prédilection en signant une bonne douzaine de best-sellers dont Vertiges ou Fièvre. Inspiré de faits réels, ce roman dénonce une médecine prise en otage par l'argent ainsi qu'une machination hélas parfaitement crédible<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/354331573?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 30, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2729086-dyana" class="user" title="Dyana">Dyana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/337156.Fatal_Cure" title="Hardcover 9780399138799" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer354331573">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16210121729070425696">Not the best from Robin Cook, but, none-the-less, an unusual premise for a story - starts out slow and builds to a fast-paced climax. Doctors Angela and David Wilson, along with their daughter Nikki, leave the urban life in Boston to relocate to the quaint small town of Bartlet, Vermont. They both find jobs at Bartlet Community Hospital, a modern state-of-the-art medical facility. This is a dream come true for Angela, a pathologist and David, an internist/primary care physician. But things turn</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16210121729070425696">Not the best from Robin Cook, but, none-the-less, an unusual premise for a story - starts out slow and builds to a fast-paced climax. Doctors Angela and David Wilson, along with their daughter Nikki, leave the urban life in Boston to relocate to the quaint small town of Bartlet, Vermont. They both find jobs at Bartlet Community Hospital, a modern state-of-the-art medical facility. This is a dream come true for Angela, a pathologist and David, an internist/primary care physician. But things turn from idyllic to horrific when many of David's new patients die from unexplained medical conditions after being hospitalized. They, also, soon discover that most of the people they meet have a great dislike for the missing former administrator of the hospital, Dr. Dennis Hodges. He was last seen drunk and ranting about former patients who had died unexpectedly from non-life threatening conditions and who were actually improving. Eight year old Nikki suffers from cystic fibrosis and seems to thrive in their new home until she is sent to the hospital with a respiratory episode that puts her life in danger. Without giving away the ending, the story centers on insurance companies and HMO's who seek a profit rather than being advocates for the patients. This story also centers on professionals with no medical background running the hospital - of course, in this book, they all seem evil and bent on the almighty profit. Hope this isn't the norm in real life!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16210121729070425696">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_180504179">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180504179" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5699299-terri-lynn" class="left imgcol" title="Terri Lynn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1329255932p2/5699299.jpg" alt="Terri Lynn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/180504179?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5699299-terri-lynn" class="user" title="Terri Lynn">Terri Lynn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/337156.Fatal_Cure" title="Hardcover 9780399138799" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5699299-terri-lynn?shelf=mystery-suspense-thrillers" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-suspense-thrillers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5699299-terri-lynn?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer180504179">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11188441934537357742">I have been a Robin Cook fan since his very first book. I recently reread this one as I am always re-reading old favorites. <br /><br />I am not quite sure what it is I love about this book but I do love it. In the small Vermont town of Bartlet, people are dying mysterious deaths at Barlet Community Hospital and retired doctor (and former hospital administrator) Dr. Hodges wants to know why. He crashes a hospital board meeting, waving the files of several of his former patients, all now dead for strange rea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11188441934537357742">I have been a Robin Cook fan since his very first book. I recently reread this one as I am always re-reading old favorites. <br /><br />I am not quite sure what it is I love about this book but I do love it. In the small Vermont town of Bartlet, people are dying mysterious deaths at Barlet Community Hospital and retired doctor (and former hospital administrator) Dr. Hodges wants to know why. He crashes a hospital board meeting, waving the files of several of his former patients, all now dead for strange reasons after staying in the hospital. After being brushed off, he walks home and someone comes to the door. He lets this person in and is beaten to death and then his body disappeared. <br /><br />Dr. Angela Wilson and Dr. David Wilson are a married couple in Boston who are just finishing up their medical residencies. Angela is a pathologist and David is a doctor of internal medicine. They have an 8 year old daughter Nikki who has cystic fibrosis. <br /><br />Since they are finishing up their residencies and need to find jobs, they have narrowed it down to three options- fellowships in Boston, academics in New York (thanks to her doctor father) or jobs in Bartlet, Vermont. In Vermont, Angela would become a pathologist at Bartlet Community Hospital and David would join the clinic practice of the HMO who insures most of the town and is the sole HMO holding up the hospital from bankruptcy. <br /><br />What David and Angela don't know is that the hospital signed a contract where the HMO pays them a set amount per year per person and that is it. The amount was too low and the hospital can't get them to raise the rate. As a result, the hospital is losing money. The board has also been skimming money off the rebuilding efforts and now need a flux of money. One of the patients who died left a 3 million dollar life insurance policy to the hospital. Also, someone is raping nurses in the parking lot but the media does not report it because the hospital asked them not to. <br /><br />There are some extremely unrealistic things that happen at this point. They had the job interviews and while Angela was being interviewed, the hospital administrator had her, David and Nikki in for the interview then walked them to the professional building for David's interview with the HMO where again, the whole family sat in on the interview. They went home thinking of the idyllic peace and quiet of the town to have trouble parking near their Boston walk up (4 flights of stairs) to find that someone had broken in and then Nikki goes to school only for there to be a 6th grade drug dealer shoot a gun on the playground near her. Cook lays it on too thick.<br /><br /><br /><br />It gets thicker when the family decides to revisit Bartlet in light of all of that. Would you believe that David and Angela decide on the spot to take the jobs because Nikki asks for a puppy and one of the townspeople offers to sell them one? Or that when they go to tell the HMO and the hospital that they send them over to the bank where the president is waiting to give them first and second mortgages with no application nor credit approval based on having the two new jobs despite the fact that they are deep in school loan debt to the tune of $150,000? And how about this- the banker sends them to a real estate agent who shows them 5 houses immediately, they settle on one, and the papers are signed, the bank mortgages are put into force, and they close on the property the same day. It just doesn't work that way in real life.<br /><br />The family is pleased to move in but small town life and work at the hospital and the HMO are anything but idyllic and soon becomes a nightmare. On his first day, David is told that the doctor who previously had his office committed suicide in it. Another doctor confides to him that it wasn't done like a suicide and in fact looked like a murder. Angela becomes victim of sexual harassment by her boss. Then the murdered body of the missing doctor is found walled in their basement but the local cops (who hated him) and the local citizens don't care and refuse to investigate. <br /><br />When Angela begins investigating, she is nearly killed in the hospital parking lot. When she hires an investigator, things take a dangerous turn for the worse. Meanwhile, 6 of David's patients who come into the hospital for things like an abcessed tooth or other problems, suddenly become ill with the same symptoms of drooling, seizures, nausea, vomiting and low white blood counts and often fever and then die. When Nikki's young friend Caroline dies there, David and Angela have to race to save Nikki's life while protecting their own.<br /><br />There is a lot of mystery, suspense, thrills and chills in this book. Small towns can hold deadly secrets. Will David, Angela, and Nikki all survive to tell the tale? </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11188441934537357742">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_126815842">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126815842" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4259066-austin" class="left imgcol" title="Austin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1289246685p2/4259066.jpg" alt="Austin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/126815842?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 18, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4259066-austin" class="user" title="Austin">Austin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/308274.Fatal_Cure" title="Unknown Binding 9780330337021" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer126815842">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15743727595962826390">I was not very fond of the book “Fatal Cure" at the beginning, but after a while it began to grow on me. This writing piece is one of those stories that move at a very slow pace with details on every individual event and setting. But don’t let this slow pace novel fool you about the fact that it can be an action packed thriller. The only problem is that the author starts off with a very dull and bland plot. I recommend this book to readers that enjoy books that a slow pace plot soon builds up to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15743727595962826390">I was not very fond of the book “Fatal Cure" at the beginning, but after a while it began to grow on me. This writing piece is one of those stories that move at a very slow pace with details on every individual event and setting. But don’t let this slow pace novel fool you about the fact that it can be an action packed thriller. The only problem is that the author starts off with a very dull and bland plot. I recommend this book to readers that enjoy books that a slow pace plot soon builds up to a huge thrilling moment that shocks the reader. At every waking point in the point the author will turn the tone and mood around and surprise us all. My wish for the author to do from now on is that he distributes the tone evenly throughout the book. Because it’s a great novel once you get to the climax, but you have to get through a lot of boring details first. And that is very tough to do. It is also one of those books that if you miss a detail then you could miss the entire book. Because this is a medical book so at the end of the day every individual detail is vital to the overall content. This book is about a husband and wife that are both doctors that move out of the urban life to a small town in Vermont. After happiness finally appearing as a result of loss of stress, a lot of unexplained deaths begin to appear. And then all the stress begins as he works as hard as possible to get to the bottom of the deaths…</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15743727595962826390">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer994980757485228684">The good thing about Cook's books is that I don't feel so guilty about reading them instead of studying. You always end up learning something. The storyline is interesting and I really liked the characters, the were outlined well. Although I have to say, it was weird reading a Cook book without his recurring pathologists, not necessarily weird in a bad way.<br /><br />On the downside, I don't think the critiche that Cook wanted to do about the American Healthcare system just fell a bit short on my opinion,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText994980757485228684">The good thing about Cook's books is that I don't feel so guilty about reading them instead of studying. You always end up learning something. The storyline is interesting and I really liked the characters, the were outlined well. Although I have to say, it was weird reading a Cook book without his recurring pathologists, not necessarily weird in a bad way.<br /><br />On the downside, I don't think the critiche that Cook wanted to do about the American Healthcare system just fell a bit short on my opinion, it got repetitive and a bit over the top sometimes. The other thing that bothered me is that I couldn't believe noone connected the dots between all the patients, so about halfway of the book I just kept being frustrated with the main character. <br /><br />It's an interesting read, not one of those books that keep you up filled with interest but it was a nice and easy read... a book to read when you're not looking to think too much.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9870728153508533281">Another classic.. A really long and good book to keep you coming back for more. The characters strike you as a little stupid because the conclusions and diagnosis is all out there. If I can figure it out, surely the doctor-couple could :). While you're waiting endlessly for this to happen, Cook has managed to unleash several nightmares, all leading up to a delicious, satisfying and a nail biting climax. <span id="freeTextContainer12281280697128468157">I got hooked on Robin Cook's novels after watching "Coma" (movie) starring Micheal Douglas Jr. and Genevieve Bujould back in 1978.<br />His novels are always a pleasing blend of professional knowledge of the medical profession, and the medics themselves--I enjoy how believable his fictional characters are.<br />Strangely with this novel, I was able to guess who the "bad guy" is, as soon as he was introduced into the storyline; and no matter how craftily and skillfully Mr. Cook introduced more suspects to mu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12281280697128468157">I got hooked on Robin Cook's novels after watching "Coma" (movie) starring Micheal Douglas Jr. and Genevieve Bujould back in 1978.<br />His novels are always a pleasing blend of professional knowledge of the medical profession, and the medics themselves--I enjoy how believable his fictional characters are.<br />Strangely with this novel, I was able to guess who the "bad guy" is, as soon as he was introduced into the storyline; and no matter how craftily and skillfully Mr. Cook introduced more suspects to muddy the waters, it was odd that I didn't get fooled this time.<br />Nonetheless, a fun medical thriller among so many he has penned!<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2180796940769213348">Bickering, dim-witted protagonists made this an annoying read. I rarely figure out mysteries early on but had this one pegged from the very first mention of the "weapon". </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5792868833945036731">Another superb medical mystery by Robin Cook. It kept me in suspense until the final pages. I never would have guessed the cause(s) of the illnesses. Plus I enjoyed how well the story flowed; it seemed effortless. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jMH5Jt9rmLY0U3qtjzif2ofPZfMhbTUisUNUIh9V0KrpFcb1LbmMTLiLDhbxWXlozjim6miwcojbSlGw08Am7w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

In an astounding debut, Spanogle takes us on an all-too-real race against time…as a young doctor enters the dark side of scientific research, desperate to stop a terrifying epidemic before it is too late….In Baltimore’s St. Raphael’s Hospital, three newly admitted patients are among society’s most helpless citizens: female residents of Baltimore’s group homes for the mentally impaired, their bodies racked by a virus the likes of which no one at St. Raphael’s has ever seen.Dr. Nathaniel McCormick is one of the first on the scene. A young investigator from the Centers for Disease Control, Nate is paid to explore the bizarre, the exotic, and the baffling–from superviruses to bioterrorism. But as soon as Nate begins to investigate the lives and habits of the victims, he knows something is terribly wrong. Using all his skills as a medical detective, Nate soon zeroes in on the “vector”–the one person who had sexual contact with the first victims. And when that suspect is found murdered, Nate fears that the disease he’s chasing may not be an act of nature, but of man.With his brash style angering his superiors and fellow investigators alike, Nate turns to an old colleague and former lover, Dr. Brooke Michaels, for help. Together the two investigators follow a twisting trail of clues to a discovery that is at once groundbreaking and unspeakable. And as a circle of treachery tightens around him, Nate is about to confront the most chilling revelation of all–and a past Nate himself has been trying to escape.At once a taut medical thriller and a riveting psychological portrait of a young doctor on the edge, Isolation Ward is a tale of runaway tension–with a brilliant “what-if” premise that is harrowing…heartbreaking…and impossible to wrench     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/19697.Robin_Cook">About Robin Cook</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/19697.Robin_Cook"><img alt="19697" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1289871734p2/19697.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer93592961721380134"><em>Librarian Note: Not to be confused with British novelist <a title="Robin Cook" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5770072.Robin_Cook">Robin Cook</a> a pseudonym of Robert William Arthur Cook.</em><br /><br />Dr. Robin Cook (born May 4, 1940 in New York City, New York) is an American doctor / novelist who writes about medicine and topics affecting public health.<br /><br />He is best known for being the author who combined medical writing with the thriller genre of writing. Several of his books have been b</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText93592961721380134"><em>Librarian Note: Not to be confused with British novelist <a title="Robin Cook" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5770072.Robin_Cook">Robin Cook</a> a pseudonym of Robert William Arthur Cook.</em><br /><br />Dr. Robin Cook (born May 4, 1940 in New York City, New York) is an American doctor / novelist who writes about medicine and topics affecting public health.<br /><br />He is best known for being the author who combined medical writing with the thriller genre of writing. Several of his books have been bestsellers on the "New York Times" Bestseller List. Several of his books have also been featured in Reader's Digest.<br /><br />Cook is a graduate of Wesleyan University and Columbia University School of Medicine. He finished his postgraduate medical training at Harvard. He divides his time between homes in Boston and Florida where he lives with his wife Barbara. He is currently on leave from the Massachusetts Eye and Ear Infirmary. He has successfully combined medical fact with fantasy to produce a succession of bestselling books. Cook's medical thrillers are designed, in part, to keep the public aware of both the technological possibilities of modern medicine and the ensuing ethical problems.<br /><br /><br />Cook got a taste of the larger world when the Cousteau Society recruited him to run its blood - gas lab in the South of France. Intrigued by diving, he later called on a connection he made through Jacques Cousteau to become an aquanaut with the US Navy Sealab when he was drafted in 1969.[1]<br /><br /><br />Cook is a private member of the Woodrow Wilson Center's Board of Trustees. The Board of Trustees, led by Chairman Joseph B. Gildenhorn, are appointed to six-year terms by the President of the United States.[2]<br /><br /><br />[edit] Doctor / Novelist<br />Dr. Cook's profession as a doctor has provided him with ideas for many of his novels. In each of his novels, he strives to write about the issues at the forefront of current medical practice.<br />To date, he has explored issues such as organ donation, genetic engineering,fertility treatment, in - vitro fertilization, research funding, managed care, drug research, and organ transplantation.[3]<br /><br /><br />Dr. Cook has been remarked to have an uncanny ability to anticipate national controversy. In an interview with Dr.Cook, Stephen McDonald talked to him about his novel Shock; Cook admits the timing of Shock was fortuitous. "I suppose that you could say that it's the most like Coma in that it deals with an issue that everybody seems to be concerned about," he says, "I wrote this book to address the stem cell issue, which the public really doesn't know anything about. Besides entertaining readers, my main goal is to get people interested in some of these issues, because it's the public that ultimately really should decide which way we ought to go in something as ethically questioning as stem cell research."[4]<br /><br /><br />Keeping his lab coat handy helps him turn our fear of doctors into bestsellers. "I joke that if my books stop selling, I can always fall back on brain surgery," he says. "But I am still very interested in it. If I had to do it over again, I would still study medicine. I think of myself more as a doctor who writes, rather than a writer who happens to be a doctor." After 23 books,he has come up with a diagnosis to explain why his medical thrillers remain so popular. "The main reason is, we all realize we are at risk. We're all going to be patients sometime," he says. "You can write about great white sharks or haunted houses, and you can say I'm not going into the ocean or I'm not going in haunted houses, but you can't say you're not going to go into a hospital."[4]</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="93592961721380134">...more</a>

    </div>
